Karpinski">Karpinski, L.C.</a> (1912). <a class="external text" href="https://zenodo.org/record/1448076" rel="nofollow">"History of Mathematics in the Recent Edition of the Encyclopædia Britannica"</a>. <i>Science</i>. <b>35</b> (888): 29–31. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bibcode_(identifier)" title="Bibcode (identifier)">Bibcode</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://ui.adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/1912Sci....35...29K" rel="nofollow">1912Sci....35...29K</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1126%2Fscience.35.888.29" rel="nofollow">10.1126/science.35.888.29</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMID_(identifier)" title="PMID (identifier)">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/17752897" rel="nofollow">17752897</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Science&amp;rft.atitle=History+of+Mathematics+in+the+Recent+Edition+of+the+Encyclop%C3%A6dia+Britannica&amp;rft.volume=35&amp;rft.issue=888&amp;rft.pages=29-31&amp;rft.date=1912&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F17752897&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1126%2Fscience.35.888.29&amp;rft_id=info%3Abibcode%2F1912Sci....35...29K&amp;rft.au=Karpinski%2C+L.C.&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fzenodo.org%2Frecord%2F1448076&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMuhammad+ibn+Musa+al-Khwarizmi"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoyer1991[httpsarchiveorgdetailshistoryofmathema00boyepage228_228]-45"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoyer1991[httpsarchiveorgdetailshistoryofmathema00boyepage228_228]_45-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFBoyer1991">Boyer 1991</a>, p. <a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/historyofmathema00boye/page/228" rel="nofollow">228</a>: "The Arabs in general loved a good clear argument from premise to conclusion, as well as systematic organization — respects in which neither Diophantus nor the Hindus excelled."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Boyer-229-46"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Boyer-229_46-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">(<a href="#CITEREFBoyer1991">Boyer 1991</a>, "The Arabic Hegemony" p. 229) "It is not certain just what the terms <i>al-jabr</i> and <i>muqabalah</i> mean, but the usual interpretation is similar to that implied in the translation above. The word <i>al-jabr</i> presumably meant something like "restoration" or "completion" and seems to refer to the transposition of subtracted terms to the other side of an equation; the word <i>muqabalah</i> is said to refer to "reduction" or "balancing" — that is, the cancellation of like terms on opposite sides of the equation."</span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-51"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-51">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFFlorian_Cajori1919"><a href="/wiki/Florian_Cajori" title="Florian Cajori">Florian Cajori</a> (1919). <a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/ahistorymathema02cajogoog" rel="nofollow"><i>A History of Mathematics</i></a>. Macmillan. p. <a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/ahistorymathema02cajogoog/page/n117" rel="nofollow">103</a>. <q>That it came from Indian source is impossible, for Hindus had no rules like "restoration" and "reduction". They were never in the habit of making all terms in an equation positive, as is done in the process of "restoration.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=A+History+of+Mathematics&amp;rft.pages=103&amp;rft.pub=Macmillan&amp;rft.date=1919&amp;rft.au=Florian+Cajori&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Farchive.org%2Fdetails%2Fahistorymathema02cajogoog&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMuhammad+ibn+Musa+al-Khwarizmi"></span></span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-68"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-68">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The full title is "The Book of the Description of the Earth, with its Cities, Mountains, Seas, All the Islands and the Rivers, written by Abu Ja'far Muhammad ibn Musa al-Khwārizmī, according to the Geographical Treatise written by Ptolemy the Claudian", although due to ambiguity in the word <i>surah</i> it could also be understood as meaning "The Book of the Image of the Earth" or even "The Book of the Map of the World".</span>
